      <p><b>San Marino</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-San_Marino.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/dd/En-us-San_Marino.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-San Marino.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>, <small>Italian:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Italian" title="Help:IPA/Italian">[sam maˈriːno]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of San Marino</b><sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-2">[2]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <i lang="it">Repubblica di San Marino</i>; <a href="/wiki/Romagnol_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Romagnol language">Romagnol</a>: <i lang="rgn">Ripóbblica d' San Marein</i>), also known as the <b><a href="/wiki/Most_Serene_Republic" title="Most Serene Republic">Most Serene Republic</a> of San Marino</b><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-2">[2]</a></sup> (Italian: <i lang="it">Serenissima Repubblica di San Marino</i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Microstate" title="Microstate">microstate</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a> completely enclosed by <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Located on the northeastern side of the <a href="/wiki/Apennine_Mountains" title="Apennine Mountains">Apennine Mountains</a>, San Marino covers a land area of just over 61&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (24&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), and has a population of 33,562.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> is the <a href="/wiki/City_of_San_Marino" title="City of San Marino">City of San Marino</a> and its largest settlement is <a href="/wiki/Dogana" title="Dogana">Dogana</a>. The capital is set at the highest point of the country on a steep mountain. San Marino's official language is <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, although <a href="/wiki/Romagnol_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Romagnol language">Romagnol</a> is the historical language and still in existence in a non-official capacity. </p>
      <p>The country derives its name from <a href="/wiki/Saint_Marinus" title="Saint Marinus">Saint Marinus</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Stonemasonry" title="Stonemasonry">stonemason</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">then Roman</a> island of <a href="/wiki/Rab" title="Rab">Rab</a>, in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>. Born in AD 275, Marinus participated in the reconstruction of <a href="/wiki/Rimini" title="Rimini">Rimini</a>'s city walls after their destruction by <a href="/wiki/Liburnians" title="Liburnians">Liburnian</a> <a href="/wiki/Pirates" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirates">pirates</a>. Marinus then went on to found an independent monastic community on <a href="/wiki/Monte_Titano" title="Monte Titano">Monte Titano</a> in AD 301; thus, San Marino lays claim to being the oldest extant sovereign state, as well as the oldest <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitutional republic">constitutional republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>San Marino's politics are ruled by <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_San_Marino" title="Constitution of San Marino">its constitution</a>, which dictates that every six months <a href="/wiki/Grand_and_General_Council" title="Grand and General Council">San Marino's parliament</a> must elect two <a href="/wiki/Captains_Regent" title="Captains Regent">Captains Regent</a>. The Captains Regent have equal powers, and are free to exercise them within the limits of the constitution and parliamentary legislation until their term expires. </p>
      <p>The country's economy is mainly based on <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Industrial_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrial sector">industry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Service_(economics)" title="Service (economics)">services</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>. It is one of the wealthiest countries in the world in terms of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">GDP per capita</a>, with a figure comparable to the most developed European regions. San Marino is considered to have a highly stable economy, with one of the lowest <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a> rates in Europe, no <a href="/wiki/National_debt" class="mw-redirect" title="National debt">national debt</a> and a budget surplus.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_San_Marino" title="History of San Marino">History of San Marino</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Marino_als_steinhauer.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Marino_als_steinhauer.png/220px-Marino_als_steinhauer.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Marino_als_steinhauer.png/330px-Marino_als_steinhauer.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Marino_als_steinhauer.png/440px-Marino_als_steinhauer.png 2x" data-file-width="458" data-file-height="334"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Marino_als_steinhauer.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Illustration of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Marinus" title="Saint Marinus">Saint Marinus</a>, the founder of the Republic of San Marino, and prominent cultural figure
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Saint_Marinus" title="Saint Marinus">Saint Marinus</a> left the island of <a href="/wiki/Rab" title="Rab">Rab</a> in present-day <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> with his lifelong friend Leo, and went to the city of <a href="/wiki/Rimini" title="Rimini">Rimini</a> as a stonemason. After the <a href="/wiki/Diocletianic_Persecution" title="Diocletianic Persecution">Diocletianic Persecution</a> following his Christian sermons, he escaped to the nearby <a href="/wiki/Monte_Titano" title="Monte Titano">Monte Titano</a>, where he built a small church and thus founded what is now the city and state of San Marino. </p>
      <p>The official founding date is 3 September 301. In 1320 the community of <a href="/wiki/Chiesanuova" title="Chiesanuova">Chiesanuova</a> chose to join the country.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In 1463 San Marino was extended with the communities of <a href="/wiki/Faetano" title="Faetano">Faetano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiorentino" title="Fiorentino">Fiorentino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montegiardino" title="Montegiardino">Montegiardino</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Serravalle_(San_Marino)" title="Serravalle (San Marino)">Serravalle</a>, after which the country's borders have remained unchanged.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1503, <a href="/wiki/Cesare_Borgia" title="Cesare Borgia">Cesare Borgia</a>, the son of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Alexander_VI" title="Pope Alexander VI">Pope Alexander VI</a> occupied the Republic for six months until his father's successor, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Julius_II" title="Pope Julius II">Pope Julius II</a>, intervened and restored the country's independence.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 4 June 1543 Fabiano di Monte San Savino, nephew of the later <a href="/wiki/Pope_Julius_III" title="Pope Julius III">Pope Julius III</a>, attempted to conquer the republic, but his infantry and cavalry failed as they got lost in a dense fog, which the Sammarinese attributed to <a href="/wiki/Quirinus_of_Sescia" title="Quirinus of Sescia">Saint Quirinus</a>, whose feast day it was.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Urbino" title="Duchy of Urbino">Duchy of Urbino</a> was annexed by the <a href="/wiki/Papal_States" title="Papal States">Papal States</a> in 1625, San Marino became an enclave within the Papal States, something which led to its seeking the formal protection of the Papal States in 1631, but this never equalled a <i>de facto</i> Papal control of the republic.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country was occupied on October 17, 1739 by the legate (Papal governor) of <a href="/wiki/Ravenna" title="Ravenna">Ravenna</a>, Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Giulio_Alberoni" title="Giulio Alberoni">Giulio Alberoni</a>, but independence was restored by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_XII" title="Pope Clement XII">Pope Clement XII</a> on 5 February 1740, the feast day of <a href="/wiki/Agatha_of_Sicily" title="Agatha of Sicily">Saint Agatha</a>, after which she became a patron saint of the republic.<sup id="cite_ref-Annio_Maria_Matteimi_2011,_p._23_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Annio_Maria_Matteimi_2011,_p._23-16">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The advance of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>'s army in 1797 presented a brief threat to the independence of San Marino, but the country was saved from losing its liberty thanks to one of its regents, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Onofri" title="Antonio Onofri">Antonio Onofri</a>, who managed to gain the respect and friendship of Napoleon. Thanks to his intervention, Napoleon, in a letter delivered to <a href="/wiki/Gaspard_Monge" title="Gaspard Monge">Gaspard Monge</a>, scientist and commissary of the French Government for Science and Art, promised to guarantee and protect the independence of the Republic, even offering to extend its territory according to its needs. The offer was declined by the regents, fearing future retaliation from other states' <a href="/wiki/Revanchism" title="Revanchism">revanchism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Giuseppe_e_Anita_Garibaldi_trovano_rifugio_a_San_Marino.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Giuseppe_e_Anita_Garibaldi_trovano_rifugio_a_San_Marino.JPG/220px-Giuseppe_e_Anita_Garibaldi_trovano_rifugio_a_San_Marino.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Giuseppe_e_Anita_Garibaldi_trovano_rifugio_a_San_Marino.JPG/330px-Giuseppe_e_Anita_Garibaldi_trovano_rifugio_a_San_Marino.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Giuseppe_e_Anita_Garibaldi_trovano_rifugio_a_San_Marino.JPG/440px-Giuseppe_e_Anita_Garibaldi_trovano_rifugio_a_San_Marino.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="421"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Giuseppe_e_Anita_Garibaldi_trovano_rifugio_a_San_Marino.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Anita_Garibaldi" title="Anita Garibaldi">Anita</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi" title="Giuseppe Garibaldi">Giuseppe Garibaldi</a> in San Marino, 1849
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:San_Marino_constitution_1600.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/San_Marino_constitution_1600.jpg/180px-San_Marino_constitution_1600.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/San_Marino_constitution_1600.jpg/270px-San_Marino_constitution_1600.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ac/San_Marino_constitution_1600.jpg 2x" data-file-width="285" data-file-height="403"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:San_Marino_constitution_1600.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The San Marino constitution, or more precisely statutes, of 1600
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the later phase of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_unification" title="Italian unification">Italian unification</a> process in the 19th century, San Marino served as a refuge for many people persecuted because of their support for unification, including <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi" title="Giuseppe Garibaldi">Giuseppe Garibaldi</a> and his wife <a href="/wiki/Anita_Garibaldi" title="Anita Garibaldi">Anita</a>. </p>
      <p>The government of San Marino made <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> President <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> an honorary citizen. He wrote in reply, saying that the republic proved that "government founded on republican principles is capable of being so administered as to be secure and enduring."<sup id="cite_ref-SanMarinoAbrahamLincoln1_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SanMarinoAbrahamLincoln1-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, when Italy declared war on <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> on 23 May 1915, San Marino remained neutral and Italy adopted a hostile view of Sammarinese neutrality, suspecting that San Marino could harbour Austrian spies who could be given access to its new radiotelegraph station. Italy tried to forcibly establish a detachment of <a href="/wiki/Carabinieri" title="Carabinieri">Carabinieri</a> in the republic and then cut the republic's telephone lines when it did not comply. Two groups of ten volunteers joined Italian forces in the fighting on the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Campaign_(World_War_I)" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Campaign (World War I)">Italian front</a>, the first as combatants and the second as a medical corps operating a Red Cross field hospital. The existence of this hospital later caused Austria-Hungary to suspend diplomatic relations with San Marino.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the war, San Marino suffered from high rates of unemployment and inflation, leading to increased tensions between the lower and middle classes. The latter, fearing that the moderate government of San Marino would make concessions to the lower class majority, began to show support for the <a href="/wiki/Sammarinese_Fascist_Party" title="Sammarinese Fascist Party">Sammarinese Fascist Party</a> (<i>Partito Fascista Sammarinese</i>, PFS), founded in 1922 and styled largely on their <a href="/wiki/Italian_Fascist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Fascist Party">Italian counterpart</a>. PFS rule lasted from 1923 to 1943, and during this time they often sought support from <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>'s fascist government in Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:A_soldier%27s_grave_in_Monte_Titano_(September_1944).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/A_soldier%27s_grave_in_Monte_Titano_%28September_1944%29.jpg/170px-A_soldier%27s_grave_in_Monte_Titano_%28September_1944%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/A_soldier%27s_grave_in_Monte_Titano_%28September_1944%29.jpg/255px-A_soldier%27s_grave_in_Monte_Titano_%28September_1944%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/A_soldier%27s_grave_in_Monte_Titano_%28September_1944%29.jpg/340px-A_soldier%27s_grave_in_Monte_Titano_%28September_1944%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="563"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:A_soldier%27s_grave_in_Monte_Titano_(September_1944).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>British troops at <a href="/wiki/Monte_Titano" title="Monte Titano">Monte Titano</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Marino" title="Battle of San Marino">Battle of San Marino</a>, September 1944
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, San Marino remained neutral, although it was wrongly reported in an article from <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> that it had declared war on the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> on 17 September 1940.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The Sammarinese government later transmitted a message to the British government stating that they had not declared war on the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-dp292_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dp292-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Three days after the fall of <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a> in Italy, PFS rule collapsed and the new government declared neutrality in the conflict. The Fascists regained power on 1 April 1944 but kept neutrality intact. Despite that, on 26 June 1944, San Marino was bombed by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>, in the belief that San Marino had been overrun by German forces and was being used to amass stores and ammunition. The Sammarinese government declared on the same day that no military installations or equipment were located on its territory, and that no belligerent forces had been allowed to enter.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> San Marino accepted thousands of civilian refugees when Allied forces went over the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Line" title="Gothic Line">Gothic Line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In September 1944, it was briefly occupied by German forces, who were defeated by Allied forces in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Marino" title="Battle of San Marino">Battle of San Marino</a>. </p>
      <p>San Marino had the world's first democratically elected <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communist</a> government – a coalition between the <a href="/wiki/Sammarinese_Communist_Party" title="Sammarinese Communist Party">Sammarinese Communist Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sammarinese_Socialist_Party" title="Sammarinese Socialist Party">Sammarinese Socialist Party</a>, which held office between 1945 and 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-Desai2006_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Desai2006-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mayne1999_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mayne1999-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>San Marino is the world's smallest <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>, although when <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a> gained independence in 1968 it challenged that claim, Nauru's <a href="/wiki/Land_mass" class="mw-redirect" title="Land mass">land mass</a> being only 21&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (8.1&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). However Nauru's jurisdiction over its surrounding waters covers 431,000&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (166,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), an area thousands of times greater than the territory of San Marino.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> San Marino became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> in 1988 and of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 1992. It is not a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, although it uses the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">Euro</a> as its currency (despite not legally being part of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>). </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_San_Marino" title="COVID-19 pandemic in San Marino">2019–20 coronavirus pandemic</a>, as of June 2020, San Marino had the highest death rate per capita of any country.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_San_Marino" title="Geography of San Marino">Geography of San Marino</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fortress_of_Guaita_2013-09-19.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Fortress_of_Guaita_2013-09-19.jpg/250px-Fortress_of_Guaita_2013-09-19.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Fortress_of_Guaita_2013-09-19.jpg/375px-Fortress_of_Guaita_2013-09-19.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Fortress_of_Guaita_2013-09-19.jpg/500px-Fortress_of_Guaita_2013-09-19.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3348" data-file-height="1842"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fortress_of_Guaita_2013-09-19.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The fortress of <i><a href="/wiki/Guaita" title="Guaita">Guaita</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/Mount_Titano" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Titano">Mount Titano</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:San_Marino_CIA_map.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/San_Marino_CIA_map.gif/220px-San_Marino_CIA_map.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a7/San_Marino_CIA_map.gif 1.5x" data-file-width="329" data-file-height="352"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:San_Marino_CIA_map.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of San Marino
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>San Marino is an <a href="/wiki/Enclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Enclave">enclave</a> (landlocked) surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> in Southern Europe, on the border between the <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Italy" title="Regions of Italy">regions</a> of <a href="/wiki/Emilia_Romagna" class="mw-redirect" title="Emilia Romagna">Emilia Romagna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marche" title="Marche">Marche</a> and about 10&nbsp;km (6.21&nbsp;mi) from the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Adriatic coast">Adriatic coast</a> at Rimini. Its hilly topography, with no flat ground, is part of the <a href="/wiki/Apennine_Mountains" title="Apennine Mountains">Apennine</a> mountain range. The highest point in the country, the summit of <a href="/wiki/Monte_Titano" title="Monte Titano">Monte Titano</a>, is 749&nbsp;m (2,457 <a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)" title="Foot (unit)">feet</a>) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>. San Marino has no still or contained <a href="/wiki/Body_of_water" title="Body of water">bodies of water</a> of any significant size. </p>
      <p>It is one of only three countries in the world to be <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">completely enclosed by another country</a> (the others being <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a>, also enclosed by Italy, and <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a>, enclosed by <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>). It is the third smallest country in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, after Vatican City and <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, and the fifth smallest country in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The terrestrial ecoregion of <a href="/wiki/Italian_sclerophyllous_and_semi-deciduous_forests" title="Italian sclerophyllous and semi-deciduous forests">Italian sclerophyllous and semi-deciduous forests</a> lies within San Marino's territory.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-32">[32]</a></sup> The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 0.01/10, ranking it last globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-33">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>San Marino lies between an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>: <i>Cfb and Cfa</i>), with some continental influences. It has warm to hot summers and cool winters, typical of inland areas of the central <a href="/wiki/Italian_Peninsula" title="Italian Peninsula">Italian Peninsula</a>. Precipitation is scattered throughout the year with no real dry month. Snowfalls are common and heavy almost every winter, especially above 400–500&nbsp;m (1,300–1,600 feet) of altitude. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_San_Marino" title="Politics of San Marino">Politics of San Marino</a>
      </div>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_San_Marino.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Parliament_San_Marino.jpg/220px-Parliament_San_Marino.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="360" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Parliament_San_Marino.jpg/330px-Parliament_San_Marino.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Parliament_San_Marino.jpg/440px-Parliament_San_Marino.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1811" data-file-height="2963"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_San_Marino.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Pubblico_(San_Marino)" title="Palazzo Pubblico (San Marino)">Palazzo Pubblico</a>, seat of the government of San Marino
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Captains_Regent_Tomassoni,_Rossi,_Mancini_and_Selva.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Captains_Regent_Tomassoni%2C_Rossi%2C_Mancini_and_Selva.jpg/220px-Captains_Regent_Tomassoni%2C_Rossi%2C_Mancini_and_Selva.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8c/Captains_Regent_Tomassoni%2C_Rossi%2C_Mancini_and_Selva.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="326" data-file-height="323"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Captains_Regent_Tomassoni,_Rossi,_Mancini_and_Selva.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Four former captains regent: from left to right, <a href="/wiki/Mirko_Tomassoni" title="Mirko Tomassoni">Mirko Tomassoni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Rossi_(politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Alessandro Rossi (politician)">Alessandro Rossi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Mancini" title="Alessandro Mancini">Alessandro Mancini</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Selva" title="Alberto Selva">Alberto Selva</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>San Marino has the political framework of a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democratic" class="mw-redirect" title="Representative democratic">representative democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Captains_regent" class="mw-redirect" title="Captains regent">captains regent</a> are both <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Heads of state">heads of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Heads of government">heads of government</a>, and there is a <a href="/wiki/Diversity_(politics)" title="Diversity (politics)">pluriform</a> <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the government and the <a href="/wiki/Grand_and_General_Council" title="Grand and General Council">Grand and General Council</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> is independent of the executive and the legislature. </p>
      <p>San Marino is considered to have the earliest written governing documents still in effect, as the Statutes of 1600 are still at the core of its constitutional framework.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>San Marino was originally led by the <a href="/wiki/Arengo" title="Arengo">Arengo</a>, initially formed from the heads of each family. In the 13th century, power was given to the Grand and General Council. In 1243, the first two captains regent were nominated by the Council. Still today, Captains Regent are elected every six months by the Council. </p>
      <p>The legislature of the republic is the Grand and General Council (<i>Consiglio grande e generale</i>). The Council is a unicameral legislature with 60 members. There are elections every five years by proportional representation in all nine administrative districts. These districts (townships) correspond to the old <a href="/wiki/Parish" title="Parish">parishes</a> of the republic. All <a href="/wiki/Citizen" class="mw-redirect" title="Citizen">citizens</a> 18 years or older are eligible to vote. </p>
      <p>Besides general legislation, the Grand and General Council approves the budget and elects the captains regent, the State Congress (composed of ten secretaries with executive power), the Council of Twelve (which forms the <a href="/wiki/Judicial_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Judicial branch">judicial branch</a> during the period of legislature of the Council), the Advising Commissions, and the Government Unions. The council also has the power to ratify treaties with other countries. The council is divided into five different Advising Commissions consisting of fifteen councilors who examine, propose, and discuss the implementation of new laws that are on their way to being presented on the floor of the council. </p>
      <p>Every six months, the council elects two captains regents to be the heads of state. The regents are chosen from opposing parties so that there is a balance of power. They serve a six-month term. The investiture of the captains regent takes place on 1 April and 1 October in every year. Once this term is over, citizens have three days in which to file complaints about the captains' activities. If they warrant it, judicial proceedings against the ex-head(s) of state can be initiated. </p>
      <p>The practice of having two heads of state, like Roman consuls, chosen in frequent elections, is derived directly from the customs of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a>. The Council is equivalent to the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Senate" title="Roman Senate">Roman Senate</a>; the captains regent, to the <a href="/wiki/Consul" title="Consul">consuls</a> of ancient <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>. It is thought the inhabitants of the area came together as Roman rule collapsed to form a rudimentary government for their own protection from foreign rule. </p>
      <p>San Marino is a multi-party democratic republic. A new election law in 2008 raised the threshold for small parties entering Parliament, causing political parties to organise themselves into two alliances: the right-wing <a href="/wiki/Pact_for_San_Marino" title="Pact for San Marino">Pact for San Marino</a>, led by the <a href="/wiki/San_Marinese_Christian_Democratic_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="San Marinese Christian Democratic Party">San Marinese Christian Democratic Party</a>; and the left-wing <a href="/wiki/Reforms_and_Freedom" title="Reforms and Freedom">Reforms and Freedom</a>, led by the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_Socialists_and_Democrats" title="Party of Socialists and Democrats">Party of Socialists and Democrats</a>, a merger of the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_San_Marino" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist Party of San Marino">Socialist Party of San Marino</a> and the former communist <a href="/wiki/Party_of_Democrats" title="Party of Democrats">Party of Democrats</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Sammarinese_general_election,_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Sammarinese general election, 2008">2008 general election</a> was won by the Pact for San Marino with 35 seats in the Grand and General Council against Reforms and Freedom's 25. </p>
      <p>On 1 October 2007, <a href="/wiki/Mirko_Tomassoni" title="Mirko Tomassoni">Mirko Tomassoni</a> was elected as among the heads of state, making him the first disabled person ever to have been elected as captain regent.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>San Marino has had more <a href="/wiki/List_of_elected_or_appointed_female_heads_of_state" class="mw-redirect" title="List of elected or appointed female heads of state">female heads of state</a> than any other country: 15 as of October 2014, including three who served twice. With regard to the legal profession, while the Order of Lawyers and Notaries of the Republic of San Marino [Ordine degli Avvocati e Notai della Repubblica di San Marino] exists, there is no clear indication as to how demographic groups have fared in the legal field. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities">Municipalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Municipalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:San_Marino.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/San_Marino.png/220px-San_Marino.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/San_Marino.png/330px-San_Marino.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/San_Marino.png/440px-San_Marino.png 2x" data-file-width="1251" data-file-height="1464"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:San_Marino.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Administrative_division" title="Administrative division">Administrative divisions</a> of San Marino
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>San Marino is divided into the following nine <a href="/wiki/Municipalities" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipalities">municipalities</a>, known locally as <i><i lang="it" title="Italian-language text">castelli</i></i> (meaning "castles"): </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/City_of_San_Marino" title="City of San Marino">San Marino</a> (City of San Marino, officially <i><i lang="it" title="Italian-language text">Città di San Marino</i></i>) is the capital.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>There are also eight minor municipalities: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Acquaviva_(San_Marino)" title="Acquaviva (San Marino)">Acquaviva</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Borgo_Maggiore" title="Borgo Maggiore">Borgo Maggiore</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Chiesanuova" title="Chiesanuova">Chiesanuova</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Domagnano" title="Domagnano">Domagnano</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Faetano" title="Faetano">Faetano</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Fiorentino" title="Fiorentino">Fiorentino</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Montegiardino" title="Montegiardino">Montegiardino</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Serravalle_(San_Marino)" title="Serravalle (San Marino)">Serravalle</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The largest settlement of the Republic is <a href="/wiki/Dogana" title="Dogana">Dogana</a>, which is not an autonomous <i><i lang="it" title="Italian-language text">castello</i></i>, but rather belongs to the Castello of <a href="/wiki/Serravalle_(San_Marino)" title="Serravalle (San Marino)">Serravalle</a>. </p>
      <p>In a similar way to an Italian <i><i lang="it" title="Italian-language text"><a href="/wiki/Comune" title="Comune">comune</a></i></i>, each <i><i lang="it" title="Italian-language text">castello</i></i> includes a main settlement, called <i><i lang="it" title="Italian-language text">capoluogo</i></i>, which is the seat of the <i><i lang="it" title="Italian-language text">castello</i></i>, and some even smaller localities known as <i><i lang="it" title="Italian-language text"><a href="/wiki/Frazione" title="Frazione">frazioni</a></i></i>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Curacies">Curacies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Curacies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The republic is made up of 43 <a href="/wiki/Parish_(administrative_division)" title="Parish (administrative division)">parishes</a><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> named <i><a href="/wiki/Curacy" class="mw-redirect" title="Curacy">curacies</a></i> (It: <i>curazie</i>):<br> <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A0_Berlone" title="Cà Berlone">Cà Berlone</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A0_Chiavello" title="Cà Chiavello">Cà Chiavello</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A0_Giannino" title="Cà Giannino">Cà Giannino</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A0_Melone" title="Cà Melone">Cà Melone</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A0_Ragni" title="Cà Ragni">Cà Ragni</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A0_Rigo" title="Cà Rigo">Cà Rigo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cailungo" title="Cailungo">Cailungo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caladino" title="Caladino">Caladino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calligaria" title="Calligaria">Calligaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canepa,_San_Marino" title="Canepa, San Marino">Canepa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capanne,_San_Marino" title="Capanne, San Marino">Capanne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Casole" title="Casole">Casole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castellaro,_San_Marino" title="Castellaro, San Marino">Castellaro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cerbaiola" title="Cerbaiola">Cerbaiola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cinque_Vie" title="Cinque Vie">Cinque Vie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Confine" title="Confine">Confine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corianino" title="Corianino">Corianino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crociale" title="Crociale">Crociale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dogana" title="Dogana">Dogana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falciano" title="Falciano">Falciano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiorina_(San_Marino)" title="Fiorina (San Marino)">Fiorina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galavotto" title="Galavotto">Galavotto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gualdicciolo" title="Gualdicciolo">Gualdicciolo</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Serra" title="La Serra">La Serra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lesignano" title="Lesignano">Lesignano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Molarini" title="Molarini">Molarini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montalbo,_San_Marino" title="Montalbo, San Marino">Montalbo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monte_Pulito" title="Monte Pulito">Monte Pulito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murata_(San_Marino)" title="Murata (San Marino)">Murata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pianacci" title="Pianacci">Pianacci</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piandivello" title="Piandivello">Piandivello</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poggio_Casalino" title="Poggio Casalino">Poggio Casalino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poggio_Chiesanuova" title="Poggio Chiesanuova">Poggio Chiesanuova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ponte_Mellini" title="Ponte Mellini">Ponte Mellini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rovereta" title="Rovereta">Rovereta</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Giovanni_sotto_le_Penne" title="San Giovanni sotto le Penne">San Giovanni sotto le Penne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Mustiola" title="Santa Mustiola">Santa Mustiola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spaccio_Giannoni" title="Spaccio Giannoni">Spaccio Giannoni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teglio,_San_Marino" title="Teglio, San Marino">Teglio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Torraccia" title="Torraccia">Torraccia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valdragone" title="Valdragone">Valdragone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valgiurata" title="Valgiurata">Valgiurata</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ventoso" title="Ventoso">Ventoso</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">September 2011</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_San_Marino" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of San Marino">Military of San Marino</a>
      </div> 
      <p>San Marino's military forces are among the smallest in the world. National defence is, by arrangement, the responsibility of <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Italy" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Italy">Italy's armed forces</a>. Different branches have varied functions, including: performing ceremonial duties; patrolling borders; mounting guard at government buildings; and assisting police in major criminal cases. The <a href="/wiki/Civil_Police_(San_Marino)" title="Civil Police (San Marino)">police</a> are not included in the military of San Marino. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Crossbow_Corps">Crossbow Corps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Crossbow Corps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Once at the heart of San Marino's army, the Crossbow Corps is now a ceremonial force of approximately 80 volunteers. Since 1295, the Crossbow Corps has provided demonstrations of <a href="/wiki/Crossbow" title="Crossbow">crossbow</a> shooting at festivals. Its uniform design is medieval. While still a statutory military unit, the Crossbow Corps has no military function today. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Guard_of_the_Rock">Guard of the Rock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Guard of the Rock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Guardia_di_Rocca_al_Palazzo_Pubblico_San_Marino.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Guardia_di_Rocca_al_Palazzo_Pubblico_San_Marino.jpg/220px-Guardia_di_Rocca_al_Palazzo_Pubblico_San_Marino.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Guardia_di_Rocca_al_Palazzo_Pubblico_San_Marino.jpg/330px-Guardia_di_Rocca_al_Palazzo_Pubblico_San_Marino.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Guardia_di_Rocca_al_Palazzo_Pubblico_San_Marino.jpg/440px-Guardia_di_Rocca_al_Palazzo_Pubblico_San_Marino.jpg 2x" data-file-width="662" data-file-height="883"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Guardia_di_Rocca_al_Palazzo_Pubblico_San_Marino.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Guardia_di_Rocca" class="mw-redirect" title="Guardia di Rocca">Guards of the Rock</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Guardia_di_Rocca" class="mw-redirect" title="Guardia di Rocca">Guard of the Rock</a> is a front-line military unit in the San Marino armed forces, a state border patrol, with responsibility for patrolling borders and defending them.<sup id="cite_ref-guidelines_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guidelines-39">[39]</a></sup> In their role as Fortress Guards they are responsible for guarding the Palazzo Pubblico in <a href="/wiki/San_Marino,_San_Marino" class="mw-redirect" title="San Marino, San Marino">San Marino City</a>, the seat of national government. </p>
      <p>In this role they are the forces most visible to tourists, and are known for their colourful ceremony of <a href="/wiki/Changing_the_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Changing the Guard">Changing the Guard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guidelines_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guidelines-39">[39]</a></sup> Under the 1987 statute the Guard of the Rock are all enrolled as "Criminal Police Officers" (in addition to their military role) and assist the police in investigating major crime. The uniform of the Guard of the Rock is a distinctive red and green.<sup id="cite_ref-guidelines_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guidelines-39">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Guard_of_the_Grand_and_General_Council">Guard of the Grand and General Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Guard of the Grand and General Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The Guard of the Grand and General Council commonly known as The Guard of the Council or locally as the "Guard of Nobles", formed in 1741,<sup id="cite_ref-guidelines_39-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guidelines-39">[39]</a></sup> is a volunteer unit with ceremonial duties. Due to its striking blue, white, and gold uniform, it is perhaps the best-known part of the Sammarinese military, and appears on countless postcard views of the republic. The functions of the Guard of the Council are to protect the <a href="/wiki/Captains_regent" class="mw-redirect" title="Captains regent">captains regent</a>, and to defend the Grand and General Council during its formal sessions. They also act as ceremonial bodyguards to government officials at both state and church festivals. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Company_of_Uniformed_Militia">Company of Uniformed Militia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Company of Uniformed Militia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In former times, all families with two or more adult male members were required to enroll half of them in the Company of Uniformed Militia. This unit remains the basic fighting force of the armed forces of San Marino, but is largely ceremonial. It is a matter of civic pride for many Sammarinese to belong to the force, and all citizens with at least six years residence in the republic are entitled to enroll. </p>
      <p>The uniform is dark blue, with a <a href="/wiki/Kepi" title="Kepi">kepi</a> bearing a blue and white plume. The ceremonial form of the uniform includes a white cross-strap, and white and blue sash, white epaulets, and white decorated cuffs. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_Ensemble">Military Ensemble</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Military Ensemble">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Formally this is part of the Army Militia,<sup id="cite_ref-guidelines_39-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guidelines-39">[39]</a></sup> and is the ceremonial military band of San Marino. It consists of approximately 60 musicians.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The uniform is similar to that of the Army Militia. Military Ensemble music accompanies most state occasions in the republic. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gendarmerie">Gendarmerie</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Gendarmerie">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Established in 1842, the <a href="/wiki/Corps_of_Gendarmerie_of_San_Marino" class="mw-redirect" title="Corps of Gendarmerie of San Marino">Gendarmerie of San Marino</a> is a militarised law enforcement agency.<sup id="cite_ref-guidelines_39-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guidelines-39">[39]</a></sup> Its members are full-time and have responsibility for the protection of citizens and property, and the preservation of law and order. </p>
      <p>The entire military corps of San Marino depends upon the co-operation of full-time forces and their retained (volunteer) colleagues, known as the <i>Corpi Militari Volontari</i>, or Voluntary Military Force. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_San_Marino" title="Economy of San Marino">Economy of San Marino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sammarinese_euro_coins" title="Sammarinese euro coins">Sammarinese euro coins</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_banks_in_San_Marino" title="List of banks in San Marino">List of banks in San Marino</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Via_Basilicus_din_San_Marino2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Via_Basilicus_din_San_Marino2.jpg/250px-Via_Basilicus_din_San_Marino2.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Via_Basilicus_din_San_Marino2.jpg/375px-Via_Basilicus_din_San_Marino2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Via_Basilicus_din_San_Marino2.jpg/500px-Via_Basilicus_din_San_Marino2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Via_Basilicus_din_San_Marino2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tourism and banking are the country's main source of revenue.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>San Marino is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> and although it is not a <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> member, it is allowed to use the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> as its currency by arrangement with the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a>; it is also granted the right to use its own designs on the national side of the <a href="/wiki/Euro_coins" title="Euro coins">euro coins</a>. Before the euro, the <a href="/wiki/Sammarinese_lira" title="Sammarinese lira">Sammarinese lira</a> was pegged to, and exchangeable with, the <a href="/wiki/Italian_lira" title="Italian lira">Italian lira</a>. The small number of <a href="/wiki/Sammarinese_euro_coins" title="Sammarinese euro coins">Sammarinese euro coins</a>, as was the case with the lira before it, are primarily of interest to <a href="/wiki/Coin_collecting" title="Coin collecting">coin collectors</a>. </p>
      <p>San Marino's per capita GDP and standard of living are comparable to that of <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>. Key industries include <a href="/wiki/Bank" title="Bank">banking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ceramic" title="Ceramic">ceramics</a>. The main <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agricultural</a> products are <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cheese" title="Cheese">cheese</a>. San Marino imports mainly staple goods from Italy. </p>
      <p>San Marino's <a href="/wiki/Postage_stamp" title="Postage stamp">postage stamps</a>, which are valid for mail posted in the country, are mostly sold to <a href="/wiki/Philately" title="Philately">philatelists</a> and are an important source of income. San Marino is no longer a member of the <a href="/wiki/Small_European_Postal_Administration_Cooperation" title="Small European Postal Administration Cooperation">Small European Postal Administration Cooperation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It has the world's highest rate of car ownership, being the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_vehicles_per_capita" title="List of countries by vehicles per capita">only country with more vehicles than people</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">Taxation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Taxation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The corporate profits tax rate in San Marino is 17%, capital gains are subject to a five percent tax, and active interest is subject to a 11% <a href="/wiki/Withholding_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Withholding tax">withholding tax</a>. Several benefits apply to new businesses, which can strongly reduce the amount of taxes to be paid. </p>
      <p>The personal income tax (IGR, Italian: <i>Imposta Generale sui Redditi</i>) was introduced in 1984 and it was heavily reformed in 2013 with the goal of increasing fiscal revenue. The nominal tax rate ranges from 9% for an annual revenue below €10,000 to 35% for revenues above €80,000. </p>
      <p>In 1972, a <a href="/wiki/Value-added_tax" title="Value-added tax">value-added tax</a> (VAT) system was introduced in Italy, and an equivalent tax was introduced also in San Marino, in accordance with the 1939 friendship treaty. However, this tax is not a standard value-added tax, but rather it is an import tax, thus, it is levied only on imported goods and raw resources. For this reason it is locally best known as single stage tax (Italian: <i>imposta monofase</i>), as it is only applied one time during importation, while VAT is applied at every exchange. Furthermore, while VAT also applies to services, the import tax only applies on physical goods. Another important difference is that while VAT is computed on the final price paid by the consumer, the import tax is levied on the importation cost paid by the company, which is generally much lower. </p>
      <p>Under the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">European Union customs agreement</a>, San Marino import tax is considered equivalent to the European VAT system. A separate tax on services, with a rate of 3%, has been introduced in 2011. The introduction of a true VAT system, not dissimilar from the European one, is under development. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_San_Marino" title="Tourism in San Marino">Tourism in San Marino</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> sector contributes over 22% of San Marino's <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-rtv_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rtv-43">[43]</a></sup> with approximately 2 million tourists having visited in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conventions_with_Italy">Conventions with Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Conventions with Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>San Marino and Italy have engaged in conventions since 1862,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> dictating some economic activities in San Marino's territory. Cultivation of tobacco and production of goods which are subject to Italy's <a href="/wiki/Government_monopoly" class="mw-redirect" title="Government monopoly">government monopoly</a> are forbidden in San Marino. Direct import is forbidden; all goods coming from a third party have to travel through Italy before reaching the country. Although it is allowed to print its own postal stamps, San Marino is not allowed to coin its own currency and is obliged to use <a href="/wiki/Istituto_Poligrafico_e_Zecca_dello_Stato" title="Istituto Poligrafico e Zecca dello Stato">Italy's mint</a>; the agreement does not affect the right of the Republic of San Marino to continue to issue gold coins denominated in Scudi<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> (legal value of 1 gold Scudo is 37.50 euros). Gambling is legal and regulated; however, casinos were outlawed prior to 2007. There is one legally operating casino. </p>
      <p>In exchange for these limitations, Italy provides San Marino with an annual stipend, and at cost, sea salt (not more than 250 tonnes per year), tobacco (40 tonnes), cigarettes (20 tonnes) and matches (unlimited amount).<sup id="cite_ref-esteri1980_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-esteri1980-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the border there are no formalities with Italy. However, at the tourist office visitors can purchase officially cancelled souvenir stamps for their <a href="/wiki/Passport" title="Passport">passports</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_San_Marino" title="Demographics of San Marino">Demographics of San Marino</a>
      </div> 
      <p>San Marino has a population of approximately 33,000, with 4,800 foreign residents, most of whom are Italian citizens. Another 12,000 Sammarinese live abroad (5,700 in Italy, 3,000 in the US, 1,900 in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and 1,600 in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>). </p>
      <p>The first census since 1976 was conducted in 2010. Results were expected by the end of 2011; however, 13% of families did not return their forms. </p>
      <p>The primary language spoken is <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>; <a href="/wiki/Romagnol_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Romagnol language">Romagnol</a> is also widely spoken. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Belluzzi" title="Giovanni Battista Belluzzi">Giovanni Battista Belluzzi</a> (1506 in San Marino – 1554) an architect</li> 
       <li><a href="https://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francesco_Maria_Marini" class="extiw" title="it:Francesco Maria Marini">Francesco Maria Marini</a> (di Pesaro) (1630–1686), a composer, playwright, and Catholic archbishop</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Antonio_Onofri" title="Antonio Onofri">Antonio Onofri</a> (1759-1825), statesman, "Father of his Country."</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Little_Tony_(singer)" title="Little Tony (singer)">Little Tony</a> (1941–2013), a pop and rock musician</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Pasquale_Valentini" title="Pasquale Valentini">Pasquale Valentini</a> (born 1953 in San Marino), a politician who has held multiple ministerial posts</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Massimo_Bonini" title="Massimo Bonini">Massimo Bonini</a> (born 1959 in San Marino), a football player who played for <a href="/wiki/Juventus" class="mw-redirect" title="Juventus">Juventus</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Marco_Macina" title="Marco Macina">Marco Macina</a> (born 30 September 1964 in San Marino), a footballer who played for <a href="/wiki/Bologna_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Bologna FC">Bologna FC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parma_Calcio_1913" title="Parma Calcio 1913">Parma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reggio_Audace_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Reggio Audace F.C.">Reggiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/AC_Milan" class="mw-redirect" title="AC Milan">AC Milan</a>.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Valentina_Monetta" title="Valentina Monetta">Valentina Monetta</a> (born 1 March 1975 in San Marino), a singer who represented San Marino four times in the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Eurovision Song Contest">Eurovision Song Contest</a></li> 
       <li>Simone Pacini (born 1981 in San Marino), a footballer who plays for local club <a href="/wiki/S.S._Folgore_Falciano_Calcio" title="S.S. Folgore Falciano Calcio">Folgore</a> as a midfielder</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Manuel_Poggiali" title="Manuel Poggiali">Manuel Poggiali</a> (born 1983 in San Marino), a Grand Prix motorcycle road racing World Champion</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Alex_De_Angelis" class="mw-redirect" title="Alex De Angelis">Alex De Angelis</a> (born 1984 in <a href="/wiki/Rimini" title="Rimini">Rimini</a>), a Grand Prix motorcycle road racer</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Davide_Simoncini" title="Davide Simoncini">Davide Simoncini</a> (born 30 August 1986 in San Marino), a footballer who plays as a defender for San Marino club <a href="/wiki/A.C._Libertas" title="A.C. Libertas">A.C. Libertas</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_national_football_team" title="San Marino national football team">San Marino national football team</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Aldo_Junior_Simoncini" title="Aldo Junior Simoncini">Aldo Junior Simoncini</a> (born 30 August 1986 in San Marino), a footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for San Marino club A.C. Libertas and San Marino national football team</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Alessandra_Perilli" title="Alessandra Perilli">Alessandra Perilli</a> (born 1988), shooting Olympian</li>

       <li><a href="/wiki/Simone_Benedettini" title="Simone Benedettini">Simone Benedettini</a> (born 1997 in San Marino), a footballer who plays as a goalkeeper</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_San_Marino" title="Religion in San Marino">Religion in San Marino</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:San_Marino_katedra.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/San_Marino_katedra.jpg/220px-San_Marino_katedra.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/San_Marino_katedra.jpg/330px-San_Marino_katedra.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/San_Marino_katedra.jpg/440px-San_Marino_katedra.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="1280"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:San_Marino_katedra.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/San_Marino_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="San Marino Cathedral">San Marino Cathedral</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>San Marino is a predominantly Catholic state<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup>—over 97% of the population profess the Roman Catholic faith, but Catholicism is not an <a href="/wiki/Established_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="Established religion">established religion</a>. Approximately half of those who profess to be Catholic practice the faith.<sup id="cite_ref-Cavendish_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cavendish-48">[48]</a></sup> There is no <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_see" title="Episcopal see">episcopal see</a> in San Marino, although its name is part of the present diocesan title. Historically, the various parishes in San Marino were divided between two Italian <a href="/wiki/Diocese" title="Diocese">dioceses</a>, mostly in the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Montefeltro" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of Montefeltro">Diocese of Montefeltro</a>, and partly in the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Rimini" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of Rimini">Diocese of Rimini</a>. In 1977, the border between <a href="/wiki/Montefeltro" title="Montefeltro">Montefeltro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rimini" title="Rimini">Rimini</a> was readjusted so that all of San Marino fell within the diocese of Montefeltro. The <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Montefeltro-San_Marino" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Montefeltro-San Marino">bishop of Montefeltro-San Marino</a> resides in <a href="/wiki/Pennabilli" title="Pennabilli">Pennabilli</a>, in Italy's province of <a href="/wiki/Pesaro_e_Urbino" class="mw-redirect" title="Pesaro e Urbino">Pesaro e Urbino</a>. </p>
      <p>There is a provision under the income tax rules that the taxpayers have the right to request for allocation of 0.3% of their income tax to the Catholic Church or to charities. The churches include the two religious groups of the <a href="/wiki/Waldensian_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Waldensian Church">Waldensian Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_San_Marino-Montefeltro" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of San Marino-Montefeltro">Roman Catholic Diocese of San Marino-Montefeltro</a> was until 1977 the historic diocese of Montefeltro. It is a <a href="/wiki/Suffragan" class="mw-redirect" title="Suffragan">suffragan</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Ravenna-Cervia" class="mw-redirect" title="Archdiocese of Ravenna-Cervia">archdiocese of Ravenna-Cervia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The diocese includes all the <a href="/wiki/Parish" title="Parish">parishes</a> of San Marino. The earliest mention of <a href="/wiki/Montefeltro" title="Montefeltro">Montefeltro</a>, as <i>Mona Feretri</i>, is in the diplomas by which <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> confirmed the <a href="/wiki/Donation_of_Pepin" title="Donation of Pepin">donation of Pepin</a>. The first known bishop of Montefeltro was Agatho (826), whose residence was at <a href="/wiki/San_Leo" title="San Leo">San Leo</a>. Under Bishop Flaminios Dondi (1724) the see was again transferred to San Leo, but later it returned to Pennabilli. The historic diocese was a suffragan of the <a href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Urbino" class="mw-redirect" title="Archdiocese of Urbino">archdiocese of Urbino</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newadvent.org_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newadvent.org-50">[50]</a></sup> Since 1988, there is formally an <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_nunciature" title="Apostolic nunciature">apostolic nunciature</a> to the republic, but it is vested in the nuncio to Italy. </p>
      <p>There has been a <a href="/wiki/Jew" class="mw-redirect" title="Jew">Jewish</a> presence in San Marino for at least 600 years.<sup id="cite_ref-JewishEncyclopedia.com_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JewishEncyclopedia.com-51">[51]</a></sup> The first mention of Jews in San Marino dates to the late 14th century, in official documents recording the business transactions of Jews. There are many documents throughout the 15th to 17th centuries describing Jewish dealings and verifying the presence of a Jewish community in San Marino.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Jews were permitted official protection by the government. </p>
      <p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, San Marino provided a haven for more than 100,000 Jews and other Italians (approximately 10 times the Sammarinese population at the time) from <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazi</a> persecution. As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, few Jews remain.<sup id="cite_ref-jewishvirtuallibrary.org_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jewishvirtuallibrary.org-53">[53]</a></sup> In 2019 there was a building inaugurated as the 'Chapel of three religions', the first ever building of its kind devoted to interfaith dialogue.<sup id="cite_ref-AJB_Video_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AJB_Video-54">[54]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="wikitable">
