      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_San_Marino" title="Transport in San Marino">Transport in San Marino</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are 220&nbsp;km (140&nbsp;mi) of roads in the country, the main road being the <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_Highway" title="San Marino Highway">San Marino Highway</a>. Authorities license private vehicles with distinctive <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_registration_plates_of_San_Marino" title="Vehicle registration plates of San Marino">Sammarinese license plates</a>, which are white with blue figures and the coat of arms, usually a letter followed by up to four numbers. Many vehicles also carry the international vehicle identification code (in black on a white oval sticker), which is "RSM". </p>
      <p>There are no public airports in San Marino, but there is a small private <a href="/wiki/Torraccia_airfield" title="Torraccia airfield">airstrip located in Torraccia</a> and an international heliport located in <a href="/wiki/Borgo_Maggiore" title="Borgo Maggiore">Borgo Maggiore</a>. Most tourists who arrive by air land at <a href="/wiki/Federico_Fellini_International_Airport" title="Federico Fellini International Airport">Federico Fellini International Airport</a> close to the city of <a href="/wiki/Rimini" title="Rimini">Rimini</a>, then make the transfer by bus. </p>
      <p>Two rivers flow through San Marino, but there is no major water transport, and no port or harbour. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>San Marino public transport comprises 8 local bus lines entirely within San Marino. Cross-border connection to Rimini is available across highway bridge in Rovereta. </p>
      <p>There is a regular bus service between Rimini and the city of San Marino that is popular with both tourists and workers commuting to San Marino from Italy. This service stops at approximately 20 locations in Rimini and within San Marino, with its two terminus stops at <a href="/wiki/Rimini_railway_station" title="Rimini railway station">Rimini railway station</a> and San Marino coach station. </p>
      <p>A limited licensed taxi service operates nationwide. There are seven licensed taxi companies operating in the republic,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> and Italian taxis regularly operate within San Marino when carrying passengers picked up in Italian territory. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:San-Marino-Gondola-1283.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/San-Marino-Gondola-1283.jpg/220px-San-Marino-Gondola-1283.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/San-Marino-Gondola-1283.jpg/330px-San-Marino-Gondola-1283.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/San-Marino-Gondola-1283.jpg/440px-San-Marino-Gondola-1283.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:San-Marino-Gondola-1283.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Aerial tramway to <a href="/wiki/Monte_Titano" title="Monte Titano">Monte Titano</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There is a 1.5&nbsp;km (0.93&nbsp;mi) aerial tramway connecting the <a href="/wiki/City_of_San_Marino" title="City of San Marino">City of San Marino</a> on top of <a href="/wiki/Monte_Titano" title="Monte Titano">Monte Titano</a> with <a href="/wiki/Borgo_Maggiore" title="Borgo Maggiore">Borgo Maggiore</a>, a major town in the republic, with the second largest population of any Sammarinese settlement. From here a further connection is available to the nation's largest settlement, <a href="/wiki/Dogana,_San_Marino" class="mw-redirect" title="Dogana, San Marino">Dogana</a>, via the local bus service. </p>
      <p>Two aerial tramway cars (gondolas) operate, with service provided at roughly 15-minute intervals throughout the day. A third vehicle is available on the system, a service car for the use of engineers maintaining the tramway. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway">Railway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Railway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ferrovia_Rimini%E2%80%93San_Marino" title="Ferrovia Rimini–San Marino">Ferrovia Rimini–San Marino</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Today, there is no railway in San Marino, but for a short period before <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, it had a single narrow-gauge line called the <a href="/wiki/Ferrovia_Rimini%E2%80%93San_Marino" title="Ferrovia Rimini–San Marino">Ferrovia Rimini–San Marino</a> which connected the country with the Italian rail network at Rimini. Because of the difficulties in accessing the capital, City of San Marino, with its mountain-top location, the terminus station was planned to be located in the village of <a href="/wiki/Valdragone" title="Valdragone">Valdragone</a>, but was extended to reach the capital through a steep and winding track comprising many tunnels. The railway was opened on 12 June 1932.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> An advanced system for its time, it was an electric railway, powered from overhead cables. It was well built and had a high frequency of passengers, but was almost completely destroyed during World War II. Many facilities such as bridges, tunnels, and stations remain visible today, and some have been converted to parks, public footpaths, or traffic routes. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1003042402">.mw-parser-output .sidebar{width:22em;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 1em;background:#f8f9fa;border:1px solid       <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pompeo_batoni_san_marino_risolleva_la_repubblica_by_stefano_bolognini.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Pompeo_batoni_san_marino_risolleva_la_repubblica_by_stefano_bolognini.JPG/200px-Pompeo_batoni_san_marino_risolleva_la_repubblica_by_stefano_bolognini.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Pompeo_batoni_san_marino_risolleva_la_repubblica_by_stefano_bolognini.JPG/300px-Pompeo_batoni_san_marino_risolleva_la_repubblica_by_stefano_bolognini.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Pompeo_batoni_san_marino_risolleva_la_repubblica_by_stefano_bolognini.JPG/400px-Pompeo_batoni_san_marino_risolleva_la_repubblica_by_stefano_bolognini.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1488" data-file-height="2037"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pompeo_batoni_san_marino_risolleva_la_repubblica_by_stefano_bolognini.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A painting in the Museo di Stato di San Marino by <a href="/wiki/Pompeo_Batoni" title="Pompeo Batoni">Pompeo Batoni</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Three_Towers_of_San_Marino" title="Three Towers of San Marino">Three Towers of San Marino</a> are located on the three peaks of <a href="/wiki/Monte_Titano" title="Monte Titano">Monte Titano</a> in the capital. They are depicted on both the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_San_Marino" title="Flag of San Marino">flag of San Marino</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Marino" class="mw-redirect" title="Coat of Arms of San Marino">coat of arms</a>. The three towers are: <i><a href="/wiki/Guaita" title="Guaita">Guaita</a></i>, the oldest of the three (it was constructed in the 11th century); the 13th-century <i><a href="/wiki/Cesta" class="mw-redirect" title="Cesta">Cesta</a></i>, located on the highest of Monte Titano's summits; and the 14th-century <i><a href="/wiki/Montale_(San_Marino)" title="Montale (San Marino)">Montale</a></i>, on the smallest of Monte Titano's summits, still privately owned. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University">University</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: University">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <i>Università degli Studi della Repubblica di San Marino</i> (<a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Republic_of_San_Marino" title="University of the Republic of San Marino">University of the Republic of San Marino</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> is the main university, which includes the <i><a href="/wiki/Scuola_Superiore_di_Studi_Storici_di_San_Marino" title="Scuola Superiore di Studi Storici di San Marino">Scuola Superiore di Studi Storici di San Marino</a></i> (Graduate School of Historical Studies), a distinguished research and advanced international study centre governed by an international Scientific Committee coordinated by the emeritus historian Luciano Canfora. Other important institutes are the <i>Istituto Musicale Sammarinese</i> (Sammarinese Musical Institute)<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Akademio_Internacia_de_la_Sciencoj_San_Marino" class="mw-redirect" title="Akademio Internacia de la Sciencoj San Marino">Akademio Internacia de la Sciencoj San Marino</a> or <i>Accademia Internazionale delle Scienze San Marino</i> (International Academy of Sciences San Marino).<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The latter is known for adopting <a href="/wiki/Esperanto_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Esperanto language">Esperanto</a> as the language for teaching and for scientific publications; further, it makes wide use of electronic <a href="/wiki/Educational_technology" title="Educational technology">educational technology</a> (also called e-learning). </p>
      <p>Italian author <a href="/wiki/Umberto_Eco" title="Umberto Eco">Umberto Eco</a> had attempted to create a "university without physical structures" in San Marino.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_San_Marino" title="Sport in San Marino">Sport in San Marino</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_at_the_Olympics" title="San Marino at the Olympics">San Marino at the Olympics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Football_in_San_Marino" title="Football in San Marino">Football in San Marino</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In San Marino <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> is the most popular sport. <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> are also popular. The three sports have their own federations, the <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_Football_Federation" title="San Marino Football Federation">San Marino Football Federation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_Basketball_Federation" title="San Marino Basketball Federation">San Marino Basketball Federation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Federazione_Sammarinese_Pallavolo" class="mw-redirect" title="Federazione Sammarinese Pallavolo">San Marino Volleyball Federation</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_national_football_team" title="San Marino national football team">San Marino national football team</a> has had little success, being made up of part-timers, never qualifying for a major tournament, and recording only one win in over 25 years of its history, a 1–0 victory in 2004 against <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein_national_football_team" title="Liechtenstein national football team">Liechtenstein</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> They have drawn four more, with their most notable result being a 1993 0–0 draw with <a href="/wiki/Turkey_national_football_team" title="Turkey national football team">Turkey</a> during the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="1994 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">European qualifiers for the 1994 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> In the same qualifying competition <a href="/wiki/Davide_Gualtieri" title="Davide Gualtieri">Davide Gualtieri</a> scored a goal 8.3 seconds into a match against <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a>; this goal held the record for the fastest in international football until 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GP_Imola2005_SchumiAlonso.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/GP_Imola2005_SchumiAlonso.jpg/220px-GP_Imola2005_SchumiAlonso.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/GP_Imola2005_SchumiAlonso.jpg/330px-GP_Imola2005_SchumiAlonso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/GP_Imola2005_SchumiAlonso.jpg/440px-GP_Imola2005_SchumiAlonso.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GP_Imola2005_SchumiAlonso.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>2005 <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_Grand_Prix" title="San Marino Grand Prix">San Marino Grand Prix</a> held in <a href="/wiki/Imola" title="Imola">Imola</a>, Italy
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> race, the <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_Grand_Prix" title="San Marino Grand Prix">San Marino Grand Prix</a>, was named after the state, although it did not take place there. Instead, it was held at the <a href="/wiki/Autodromo_Enzo_e_Dino_Ferrari" class="mw-redirect" title="Autodromo Enzo e Dino Ferrari">Autodromo Enzo e Dino Ferrari</a> in the Italian town of <a href="/wiki/Imola" title="Imola">Imola</a>, about 100&nbsp;km (60&nbsp;mi) northwest of San Marino. <a href="/wiki/Roland_Ratzenberger" title="Roland Ratzenberger">Roland Ratzenberger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ayrton_Senna" title="Ayrton Senna">Ayrton Senna</a> suffered fatal accidents a day apart during the <a href="/wiki/1994_San_Marino_Grand_Prix" title="1994 San Marino Grand Prix">1994 Grand Prix</a>. This international event was removed from the calendar in <a href="/wiki/2007_Formula_One_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Formula One season">2007</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_and_Rimini%27s_Coast_motorcycle_Grand_Prix" class="mw-redirect" title="San Marino and Rimini's Coast motorcycle Grand Prix">San Marino and Rimini's Coast motorcycle Grand Prix</a> was reinstated in the schedule in 2007 and takes place at the <a href="/wiki/Misano_World_Circuit_Marco_Simoncelli" title="Misano World Circuit Marco Simoncelli">Misano World Circuit Marco Simoncelli</a>, as does San Marino's round of the <a href="/wiki/World_Superbike_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="World Superbike Championship">World Superbike Championship</a>. </p>
      <p>San Marino has <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_(baseball_team)" class="mw-redirect" title="San Marino (baseball team)">a professional baseball team</a> which plays in <a href="/wiki/Italian_Baseball_League" title="Italian Baseball League">Italy's top division</a>. It has participated in the <a href="/wiki/European_Cup_(baseball)" title="European Cup (baseball)">European Cup</a> tournament for the continent's top club sides several times, hosting the event in 1996, 2000, 2004, and <a href="/wiki/2007_European_Cup_(baseball)" title="2007 European Cup (baseball)">2007</a>. It won the championship in 2006 and was a runner-up in <a href="/wiki/2010_European_Cup_(baseball)" title="2010 European Cup (baseball)">2010</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Together with Italy, San Marino held the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_European_Under-21_Championship" title="2019 UEFA European Under-21 Championship">2019 UEFA European Under-21 Championship</a>, with teams playing at the <a href="/wiki/Stadio_Olimpico_(San_Marino)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stadio Olimpico (San Marino)">Stadio Olimpico</a> in <a href="/wiki/Serravalle_(San_Marino)" title="Serravalle (San Marino)">Serravalle</a>. </p>
      <p>San Marino has had <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_at_the_Olympics" title="San Marino at the Olympics">little success</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>, winning no medals. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sammarinese_cuisine" title="Sammarinese cuisine">Sammarinese cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Piadina.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Piadina.jpg/200px-Piadina.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Piadina.jpg/300px-Piadina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Piadina.jpg/400px-Piadina.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2088" data-file-height="2052"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Piadina.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <i><a href="/wiki/Piadina" title="Piadina">piadina</a></i>, a dish characteristic of the Italian region of Romagna and of its enclave of San Marino
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The cuisine of San Marino is extremely similar to <a href="/wiki/Italian_cuisine" title="Italian cuisine">Italian</a>, especially that of the adjoining <a href="/wiki/Emilia-Romagna" title="Emilia-Romagna">Emilia-Romagna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marche" title="Marche">Marche</a> regions, but it has a number of its own unique dishes and products. Its best known is probably the <i><a href="/wiki/Torta_Tre_Monti" title="Torta Tre Monti">Torta Tre Monti</a></i> ("Cake of the Three Mountains" or "Cake of the Three Towers"), a wafer layered cake covered in chocolate depicting the <a href="/wiki/Three_Towers_of_San_Marino" title="Three Towers of San Marino">Three Towers of San Marino</a>. The country also has a small <a href="/wiki/Sammarinese_wine" title="Sammarinese wine">wine</a> industry. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UNESCO">UNESCO</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: UNESCO">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The site San Marino: Historic Centre and Mount Titano became part of the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> World Heritage List in 2008. The decision was taken during the 32nd Session of the UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Committee" title="World Heritage Committee">World Heritage Committee</a> composed of 21 Countries convened in Québec, Canada. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_San_Marino" title="Music of San Marino">Music of San Marino</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_in_the_Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="San Marino in the Eurovision Song Contest">San Marino in the Eurovision Song Contest</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The country has a long and rich musical tradition, closely linked to that of Italy, but which is also highly independent in itself. A well-known 17th-century composer is Francesco Maria Marini. The pop singer <a href="/wiki/Little_Tony_(singer)" title="Little Tony (singer)">Little Tony</a> achieved considerable success in the United Kingdom and Italy in the 1950s and 1960s. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/San_Marino_in_the_Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="San Marino in the Eurovision Song Contest">San Marino</a> has taken part in the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Eurovision Song Contest">Eurovision Song Contest</a> ten times, achieving two final qualifications to date (with then-three, eventually four-time contestant and San Marino native <a href="/wiki/Valentina_Monetta" title="Valentina Monetta">Valentina Monetta</a> with "<a href="/wiki/Maybe_(Valentina_Monetta_song)" title="Maybe (Valentina Monetta song)">Maybe</a>" in <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2014" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2014">2014</a> and Turkish singer <a href="/wiki/Serhat_(singer)" title="Serhat (singer)">Serhat</a> with "<a href="/wiki/Say_Na_Na_Na" title="Say Na Na Na">Say Na Na Na</a>" who achieved 19th place in the final in <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2019" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2019">2019</a>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_holidays_and_festivals">Public holidays and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marino&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Public holidays and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

             <ul>
              <li><sup>1</sup> <a href="/wiki/Island#Oceanic_islands" title="Island">Oceanic islands</a> within the vicinity of Europe are usually grouped with the continent even though they are not situated on its continental shelf.</li>
              <li><sup>2</sup> Some countries completely outside the conventional geographical boundaries of Europe are commonly associated with the continent due to ethnological links.</li>
